COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214, “An Act to Make 9 
Supplemental Appropriations and Allocations for the Expenditures of State Government, 10 
General Fund and Other Funds and to Change Certain Provisions of the Law Necessary to 11 
the Proper Operations of State Government for the Fiscal Years Ending June 30, 2024 and 12 
June 30, 2025” 13 
Amend the bill by striking out everything after the enacting clause and inserting the 14 
following: 15

Sec. C-4. Authorization of payments. If the State's continued obligation for any 17 
individual component contained in those sections of this Part that set the total cost of 18 
funding public education from kindergarten to grade 12 and the local and state 19 
contributions for that purpose exceeds the level of funding provided for that component, 20 
any unexpended balances occurring in other programs may be applied to avoid proration 21 
of payments for any individual component. Any unexpended balances from this Part may 22 
not lapse but must be carried forward for the same purpose.23 
Sec. C-5. Limit of State's obligation. Those sections of this Part that set the total 27 
cost of funding public education from kindergarten to grade 12 and the local and state 28 
contributions for that purpose may not be construed to require the State to provide payments 29 
that exceed the appropriation of funds for general purpose aid for local schools for the fiscal 30 
year beginning July 1, 2024 and ending June 30, 2025. 31

PART E39 
Sec. E-1.  32 MRSA §15224, as amended by PL 2001, c. 573, Pt. B, §28 and affected 10 
by §36, is further amended to read: 11 
§15224.  Installation of new elevators and tramways; fees 12 
Detailed plans or specifications of each new or altered elevator or tramway must be 13 
submitted to and appro ved by the chief inspector before the construction may be started. 14 
Fees for examination of the plans or specifications must be set by the director under section 15 
15225‑A. For the purposes of this section, fees may not exceed 1.5% of the cost of the new 16 
or altered elevator or tramway. 17 
Sec. E-2.  32 MRSA §15225-A, as amended by PL 2013, c. 70, Pt. D, §28, is further 18 
amended to read: 19 
§15225-A.  Fees 20 
The director may establish by rule fees for purposes authorized under this chapter in 21 
amounts that are reasonable and necessary for their respective purposes, except that the fee 22 
for any one purpose, other than permit and inspection fees and fees set for the purposes of 23 
section 15224, may not exceed $500.  Rules adopted pursuant to this section are routine 24

Sec. H-24.  36 MRSA §1819, sub-§2, as amended by PL 2021, c. 181, Pt. B, §6, is 21 
further amended to read: 22 
2.  Sourcing for sales of tangible personal property and taxable services; generally.  23 
The sale of tangible personal property or a taxable service is sourced in this State pursuant 24 
to this subsection.  Except as provided in subsections 3 to 5, the provisions of this 25 
subsection do not apply to the lease or rental of tangible personal property. 26 
A.  When the tangible personal property or taxable service is received by the purchaser 27 
at a business location of the seller, the sale is sourced to that business location. 28 
B.  When the tangible personal property or taxable service is not received by the 29 
purchaser at a business location of the seller, the sale is sourced to the location where 30 
receipt by the purchaser or the purchaser's donee occurs, including the location 31 
indicated by instructions for delivery to the purchaser or donee known to the seller. 32 
C.  For a sale when paragraphs A and B do not apply, the sale is sourced to the location 33 
indicated by an address for the purchaser that is available from the business records of 34 
the seller that are maintained in the ordinary course of the seller's business when use of 35 
this address does not constitute bad faith. 36 
D.  For a sale when paragraphs A to C do not apply, the sale is sourced to the location 37 
indicated by an address for the purchaser obtained during the consummation of the 38 
sale, including the address of a purchaser's payment instrument, if no other address is 39 
available, when use of this address does not constitute bad faith. 40 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 159 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
E.  When paragraphs A to D do not apply, including the circumstance in which the 1 
seller is without sufficient information to apply paragraphs A to D, the location is 2 
determined by the address from which tangible personal property was shipped, from 3 
which the tangible personal property or taxable service transferred electronically was 4 
first available for transmission by the seller or from which the service was provided, 5 
disregarding for these purposes any location that merely provided the digital transfer 6 
of the tangible personal property or taxable service sold. 7

Sec. H-28.  36 MRSA §2022 is enacted to read: 22 
§2022.  Refund of sales and use tax on purchases of qualifying retail lease or rental 23 
property 24 
1.  Definitions.  For purposes of this section, unless the context otherwise indicates, 25 
the following terms have the following meanings. 26 
A.  "Qualified lessor" means a person who: 27 
(1)  Paid Maine sales or use tax on the purchase of qualifying lease or rental 28 
property on or after January 1, 2023 and before January 1, 2025; and 29 
(2)  Collected and remitted Maine sales or use tax on the lease or rental of 30 
qualifying lease or rental property on or after January 1, 2025. 31 
B.  "Qualifying lease or rental property" means tangible personal property: 32 
(1) Upon the purchase of which a qualified lessor paid Maine sales or use tax on 33 
or after January 1, 2023 and before January 1, 2025; and 34 
(2)  That was part of a taxable lease or rental transaction on or after January 1, 2025 35 
for which the qualified lessor of the property collected and remitted Maine sales or 36 
use tax to the State.  37 
2.  Refund authorized.  The State Tax Assessor shall refund the tax imposed pursuant 38 
to this Part and paid by a qualified lessor on the purchase of qualifying lease or rental 39 
property on or after January 1, 2023 and before January 1, 2025.  The amount of the refund 40 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 161 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
for qualifying lease or rental property is limited to the Maine sales or use tax collected and 41 
remitted to the State by the qualified lessor on qualifying lease or rental property on or after 42 
January 1, 2025 and before January 1, 2027.43 
3.  Procedure and limitation.  A qualified lessor may request a refund on qualifying 4 
lease or rental property by submitting a claim for refund on a form prescribed by the 5 
assessor.  In order to qualify for a refund under this section, a qualified lessor must file one 6 
claim for all qualifying lease or rental property and must file the claim on or after January 7 
1, 2027 and before March 31, 2027. 8 
4.  Audit.  The assessor may audit a claim for re fund filed under this section.  If the 9 
assessor determines that the amount of refund is incorrect, the assessor may issue an 10 
assessment within 3 years from the date the claim was filed or at any time if a fraudulent 11 
claim was filed.  The claimant may seek reconsideration of the assessment pursuant to 12 
section 151. 13

of lease or rental payments, each time period for which a lease or rental payment is charged 16

PART N 7 
Sec. N-1.  5 MRSA §3360, sub-§5-A is enacted to read: 8 
5-A.  Mass violence crime.  "Mass violence crime" means an intentional violent crime 9 
that results in physical, emotional or psychological injury to a large number of individuals 10 
and significantly increases the burdens on victim support and the crime victims' 11 
compensation program. 12 
Sec. N-2.  5 MRSA §3360 -E, as amended by PL 1999, c. 360, §7 and affected by 13 
§9 and amended by c. 731, Pt. QQQ, §§1 and 2, is repealed and the following enacted in 14 
its place: 15 
§3360-E.  Payment of awards; limits 16 
Payments from the fund and limits on those payments are governed by this section. 17 
1.  Compensation for victim of sexual assault or other specified crime.  The board 18 
may award compensation to a claimant of up to $15,000 for actual and unreimbursed losses 19 
and eligible expenses of any person who is sexually assaulted or who suffers personal injury 20 
or death as the result of a crime specified in section 3360, subsection 3. 21 
2.  Payment to victim of mass violence crime; source of payments.  Notwithstanding 22 
the compensation limits in subsection 1, if the underlying crime is a mass violence crime, 23 
the board may award a total amount of compensation of more than $15,000.  Any awarded 24 
amount in excess of $15,000 must be paid from the Maine Mass Violence Care Fund 25 
established in section 3360-W. 26 
3.  Award for family or household member.  An award of compensation for the 27 
benefit of a family or household member is derivative of the claim of the victim.  The total 28 
compensation paid from the fund for all claims arising from the crime against the victim 29 
may not exceed $15,000. 30 
4.  Payment to individuals responsible for medical, funeral and other expenses of 31 
victim.  Within the limits specified in this section, when a person dies as the direct result 32 
of a specified crime under section 3360, subsection 3, any individual who pays or who is 33 
legally responsible for medical, medically related, funeral or burial expenses may seek 34 
compensation for those unreimbursed expenses incurred by the individual.  A provider of 35 
medical or funeral services may not seek reimbursement directly. 36 
5.  Method of payment of award.  The board, in its sole discretion, may disburse 37 
funds awarded directly to th e claimant or to the individuals or entities who provided the 38 
services for which compensation was awarded.  In the case of more than one family or 39 
household member, the board may apportion the total compensation as the board 40 
determines. 41 
Sec. N-3.  5 MRSA c. 316-D is enacted to read: 42 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 164 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
CHAPTER 316-D 1 
MAINE MASS VIOLENCE CARE FUND 2 
§3360-W.  Maine Mass Violence Care Fund 3 
1.  Fund established; pu rpose; source of funds.  The Maine Mass Violence Care 4 
Fund, referred to in this chapter as "the fund," is established within the Department of the 5 
Attorney General as an Other Special Revenue Funds account. The purpose of the fund is 6 
to provide a sustainabl e source of funds for expenses eligible for reimbursement by the 7 
Victims' Compensation Board established under section 3360 -A arising from a mass 8 
violence crime pursuant to chapter 316 -A that are not paid for by insurance or any other 9 
source. The fund is funded through appropriations and allocations and may receive private 10 
donations and federal and state funds designated by law for the payment of claims and 11 
reasonable administrative costs of the fund. Eligible investment earnings credited to the 12 
assets of the fund become part of the assets of the fund. 13 
2.  Administration and investment of fund. The fund is administered by the Treasurer 14 
of State in accordance with this subsection. 15 
A. In consultation with the Attorney General, the Treasurer of State may hold, invest, 16 
reinvest and manage the fund in a manner that fulfills the purpose of the fund as long 17 
as the investment and reinvestment of funds is in compliance with section 138 and the 18 
Maine Uniform Trust Code, including the Maine Uniform Prudent Investor Act. 19 
B. All costs of administering the fund, including the necessary and proper expenses 20 
incurred by the Treasurer of State in administering the fund, must be paid from the 21 
fund. 22 
C.  The Treasurer of State, the Attorney General and the Victims' Compensation Board 23 
established in section 3360-A may not encumber, invest, divest or disburse funds for 24 
any purpose not specifically included in this section. 25 
3.  Distributions from fund.  The Victims' Compensation Board established under 26 
section 3360-A shall make distributions from the fund in accordance with chapter 316 -A 27 
and rules establishing eligibility criteria adopted by the board. 28 
A.   Only gains, interest, dividends and other revenue earned on funds in the fund and 29 
any amounts gifted to the fund may be expended. 30 
B. Payments from the fund to a victim for eligible expenses, as set forth in section 31 
3360-E, may not be made sooner than 3 years after the applicable mass violence crime. 32 
4.  Rules. The board may adopt rules to implement the provisions of this section 33 
including establishing eligibility criteria. 34 
5.  Annual report. The Attorney General and the Treasurer of State shall report to the 35 
joint standing committee of the Legislature h aving jurisdiction over judiciary matters by 36 
February 1st of each year regarding implementation of the fund, including procedures 37 
developed by the Victims' Compensation Board, total revenue available for reimbursement 38 
of eligible claims and annual expenditures from the fund. 39 
Sec. N-4.  Working group on Maine Mass Violence Care Fund.  The Working 40 
Group to Recommend any Changes to Eligibility Standards for Expenditures from the 41 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 165 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
Maine Mass Violence Care Fund, referred to in this section as "the working group," is 42 
established.43 
1. Definitions.  As used in this section, unless the co ntext otherwise indicates, the 3 
following terms have the following meanings.  4 
A. "Board" means the Victims' Compensation Board established in the Maine Revised 5 
Statutes, Title 5, section 3360-A.  6 
B. "Eligible expenses" means expenses that are determined by the board to be eligible 7 
for reimbursement from the fund as of May 1, 2024.  8 
C. "Family or household member" has the same meaning as in the Maine Revised 9 
Statutes, Title 5, section 3360, subsection 5. 10 
D. "Mass violence crime" means an intentional violent c rime that results in physical, 11 
emotional or psychological injury to a large number of individuals and that 12 
significantly increases the burdens on victim support and compensation systems in the 13 
jurisdiction in which the violent crime occurred.  14 
E. "Victim" has the same meaning as in the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 5, section 15 
200-E, subsection 1, paragraph B. 16 
2. Purpose of working group.  The purpose of the working group is to identify and 17 
recommend to the board and the Legislature  any changes regarding specific options and 18 
eligibility criteria to help ensure that those individuals adversely affected by a mass 19 
violence crime are provided some financial relief from physical and behavioral health care 20 
costs not paid for from another public or private source, in cluding, but not limited to, the 21 
MaineCare program, Medicaid or private insurance.  Specifically, the working group shall 22 
consider and make recommendations regarding: 23 
A. Gaps in payments for physical and behavioral health care services for victims of 24 
mass violence crimes; 25 
B. Methods of investing the funds in the fund to ensure sustainable annual financial 26 
returns;  27 
C. Options for determining eligibility for distributions from the fund, including any 28 
changes regarding parameters for:  29 
(1) Who is considered a victim of a mass violence crime;  30 
(2) Which health care costs are considered eligible expenses; and 31 
(3) What constitutes a mass violence crime; and  32 
D. Anything else the working group determines necessary to carry out the purposes of 33 
the fund.  34 
3. Membership; chair; appointments. The working group consists of the following 35 
members:  36 
A. A member of the Senate, appointed by the President of the Senate;  37 
B. A member of the House of Representatives, appointed by the Speaker of the House;  38 
C. The Attorney General or the Attorney General's designee;  39 
D. The Commissioner of Health and Human Services or the commissioner's designee;  40 
1 
2

COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
E. The Treasurer of State or the Treasurer of State's designee; and  1 
F. The chair of the board or the chair's designee. 2 
The member of the Senate and the member of the House of Representatives serve as 3 
cochairs.  4 
All appointments must be made within 30 days following the effective date of this Part. 5 
4. Report. The working group under subsection 2 shall provide its recommendations 6

PART T 36 
Sec. T-1. Department of Public Safety to establish public safety health and 37 
wellness grant pilot program.    The Department of Public Safety shall establish a 38 
2-year public safety health and wellness grant pilot program, referred to in this Part as "the 39 
pilot program," to provide grants to government entities for the purpose of providing public 40 
safety employees with wellness visits or specialized cardiac and metabolic screenings that 41 
specifically address the physical or mental health effects experienced by public safety 42 
employees.  Services provided under the pilot program may not supplant existing 43 
1 
2 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 168 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
behavioral, mental or physical health care benefit packages and must supplement existing 44 
programs.  For the purposes of this Part, the following terms have the following meanings.45 
1.  "Government entity" means the State or a municipality, plantation or county. 3 
2.  "Public safety agency" means a department or other agency of a government entity 4 
that provides or has the authority to provide fire, emergency medical, emergency 5 
communications, correctional or police services. 6 
3.  "Public safety employee" means an employee of a public safety agency. 7 
Sec. T -2. Programs to address p hysical and mental health effects 8 
experienced by public safety employees.   A government entity may apply for a grant 9 
under the pilot program for any group of public safety employees as long as services are 10 
provided to all public safety employees of the pu blic safety agency within that group, 11 
wherever located.  Applications by a government entity must include at least one of the 2 12 
following screening programs: 13 
1.  Specialized cardiac and metabolic screening that provides a medical consultation 14 
and an indivi dualized plan including nutrition, fitness and wellness recommendations to 15 
the employee when appropriate.  The results of the screening and any advice for the 16 
continued treatment of identified health issues must be provided to the employee and the 17 
employee's physician.  Testing must include the following: 18 
A.  An advanced lipid panel, including a cardiac inflammatory biomarker analysis; 19 
B.  Screening for liver and kidney function; 20 
C.  Screening for thyroid, prostate and other cancers or diseases that are pre valent 21 
among first responders at a higher rate than the civilian population, such as diabetes; and 22 
D.  Cardiologist-guided, public safety-specific, cardio-metabolic stress testing; and 23 
2.  Annual wellness visits that provide confidential visits with qualified mental health 24 
professionals who have experience with the cumulative impact of exposure to traumatic 25 
events and specialized knowledge of public safety psychology.  Options for referrals to 26 
additional counseling services, inpatient services or specialist s for the participating 27 
employee or employee's immediate family must be available.    28 
Unless otherwise provided by law, services provided under this section may not be 29 
used as a basis for employment termination. 30 
Sec. T -3. Confidentiality.   All health care  information of an employee is 31 
confidential as provided in the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 22, section 1711 -C.  If 32 
wellness visits are mandated as a condition of employment by a public safety agency, only 33 
confirmation of attendance may be shared by a health care provider with the agency. 34 
Sec. T-4. Administration costs.  A government entity that receives a grant under 35 
the pilot program may use up to 10% of the grant funding to administer the grant. 36 
Sec. T-5. Reporting.  The Department of Public Safety shall ensure that government 37 
entities receiving grants provide to the department detailed anonymized information on the 38 
number of public safety employees who participated in the pilot program, the types of 39 
services provided to those employees and any outcome data that can be provided to show 40 
effectiveness of the pilot program.  The Department of Public Safety shall submit a report 41 
no later than January 10, 2026 to the joint standing committee of the Legislature having 42 
1 
2

Page 169 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
jurisdiction over health and human services matters and the joint standing committee of the 43 
Legislature having jurisdiction over criminal justice and public safety matters with the 44 
number of grants disbursed, the number of public safety employees served , the types of 45 
services provided and outcome data on the effectiveness of the program.46

Sec. W-17.  20-A MRSA §7209-A is enacted to read: 1 
§7209-A.  Transition of responsibility for ensuring a free, appropriate public 2 
education for children eligible under Part B, Section 619 3 
In order to meet the requirement that, beginning July 1, 2028, all school administrative 4 
units are designated as responsible for child find activities and for ensuring a free, 5 
appropriate public education for children eligible under Part B, Section  619 pursuant to 6 
section 7006, the following transition schedule and supports apply. 7 
1. Transition year one.  Beginning July 1, 2024, school administrative units may be 8 
approved by the commissioner to assume the responsibility for child find activities and for 9 
ensuring a free, appropriate public education for children eligible under Part B, Section 10 
619. The department shall approve readiness plans in accordance with subsection 8 and 11 
shall provide professional learning in working with young children and their  families and 12 
technical support throughout the planning and implementation of the first year to assist 13 
school administrative units to prepare to meet the standards of the readiness plans. Funding 14 
must be provided to school administrative units on a quarter ly basis in accordance with 15 
section 7303. Prior to a school administrative unit assuming responsibilities for child find 16 
activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education, the department shall 17 
establish a memorandum of understanding with the school administrative unit to determine 18 
the services to be provided by the department and the regional support and service hub. 19 
The memorandum of understanding must be reviewed and updated in response to 20 
unanticipated needs each month.  The department sha ll contract with a national expert to 21 
regularly monitor funding and programming and recommend changes to be considered as 22 
part of the transition year one activities.  23 
2. Additional transition years.  During the 2025 -2026, 2026 -2027 and 2027 -2028 24 
school years, the commissioner shall approve school administrative units in addition to 25 
those approved under subsection 1 to assume responsibility for child find activities and for 26 
ensuring a free, appropriate public education. The department shall provide profession al 27 
learning, funding and technical assistance in the same manner as provided to school 28 
administrative units in subsection 1.  29 
3. Additional time for certain school administrative units.  If the commissioner 30 
determines that a school administrative unit is no t able to assume responsibility for child 31 
find activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education by July 1, 2028 because 32 
the school administrative unit requires additional time and support in regions where related 33 
services and staffing are n ot available to support the transition, the commissioner shall 34 
provide that school administrative unit with necessary resources and an additional year to 35 
assume responsibility for child find activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public 36 
education. If the school administrative unit cannot assume responsibility for child find 37 
activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education, as determined by the 38 
commissioner, the school administrative unit may qualify for a modified plan for managing 39 
children eligible under Part B, Section 619 in accordance with section 7006, subsection 4. 40 
4.  Service provision. A school administrative unit that has assumed responsibility for 41 
child find activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education may directly 42 
provide special education and related services to children eligible under Part B, Section 43 
619, may contract with public and private providers to provide special education and related 44 
services and may access the school administrative unit's regional site or regional support 45

and service hub to provide certain services as delineated in the memorandum of 46

underserved through the Child Development Services System. The Child Development 25

provided. The review must be conducted for children eligible under Part B, Section 619: 28 
A. Who are entering kindergarten; and 29

to a school administrative unit. For children eligible under this subsection, the review 31 
must be conducted prior to the school administrative unit  assuming responsibility for 32 
child find activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education.  33 
If legally required special education and related services have not been provided or have 34 
only partially been provided, the Child Development Service s System shall schedule an 35 
individualized education program meeting to determine the compensatory services that are 36 
warranted and to develop a plan to provide necessary compensatory services.   37

A. The requirements for bas ic approval standards for public preschool programs 43 
established by applicable department rule; 44

Sec. W-18.  20-A MRSA §7211 is enacted to read: 1 
§7211.  Regional support and service hubs 2 
The Child Development Services System shall establish 9 regional support and service 3 
hubs that are aligned with each of the 9 superintendent regions established by the statewide 4 
association of superintendents. The regional support and service hubs shall provide 5 
supports and resources to school administrative units that have assumed the responsibility 6 
for child find activities and for providing a fre e, appropriate public education to children 7 
eligible under Part B, Section 619 pursuant to section 7006, subsection 2 and other high -8 
quality early childhood programs partnering with or otherwise contracted by a school 9 
administrative unit to fulfill the sch ool administrative unit's responsibilities under Part B, 10 
Section 619 pursuant to section 7006, subsection 2 as determined through memoranda of 11 
understanding between the department and the school administrative unit.  12 
1. Minimum requirements. Each regional support and service hub shall, at a 13 
minimum, offer the following supports, assistance and resources to the school 14 
administrative units within the superintendent region to which the regional support and 15 
service hub is aligned: 16 
A.  Assistance with child find activities; 17 
B. Training and other professional development opportunities and technical assistance 18 
with the implementation of developmentally appropriate practices for young children, 19 
including, but not limited to, curriculum, screening and assessment sele ctions aligned 20 
with the State's early learning developmental standards, understanding of and 21 
requirements to meet free, appropriate public education and least restrictive 22 
environment standards and best practices for inclusive learning; 23 
C. Assistance with e stablishing and strengthening community partnerships with 24 
existing inclusive, high-quality early childhood programs to help school administrative 25 
units meet federal obligations under Part B, Section 619. High-quality early childhood 26 
programs include, but are not limited to, Head Start programs, private prekindergarten 27 
and child care programs and other community-based programs; 28 
D. Assistance with locating transportation services; 29 
E. Assistance with administrative tasks associated with the assumption of 30 
responsibility for a free, appropriate public education under Part B, Section 619; and 31 
F. Maintenance and coordination of access to credentialed educators and service 32 
providers who are available to school administrative units on a contractual basis, 33 
including, but not limited to, supportive educational technicians; speech, occupational 34 
and physical therapists; assistive technology experts; and board -certified behavioral 35 
experts. 36

units that have assumed the responsibility for child find activities and for ensuring a free, 38

restrictive environment, the regional support and service hubs shall: 40 
A.  Ensure that parents of children eligible under Part B, Section 619 are recognized as 41 
collaborative partners, experts and decision makers;  42

Sec. W-19.  20-A MRSA §7303 is enacted to read: 22 
§7303.  Per-pupil rate for children eligible under Part B, Section 619 23 
Funding for school administrative units that assume responsibility for child find 24 
activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education for children eligible under 25 
Part B, Section 619 pursuant to section  7006, subsection 2 may not be appropriated to or 26 
allocated through general purpose aid for local schools and must be provided at 100% state 27 
share. This funding must be calculated by the commissioner as follows. 28 
1. Per-pupil operating allocation.   The per -pupil operating allocation for children 29 
eligible under Part B, Section 619 must be calculated on a per -pupil basis in the same 30 
manner by which operating allocations are generated in sections 15674, 15675 and 15681.  31 
2. Preschool special education and related services allocation. The preschool special 32 
education and related services per-pupil allocation must be calculated annually for children 33 
eligible under Part B, Section 619 at the EPS per-pupil rate for each school administrative 34 
unit under section 15676,  multiplied by 1.5, for each eligible resident student. This 35 
allocation must be paid at the start of each quarter, based on the estimated student count on 36 
July 1st and adjusted to reflect actual counts on October 1st, with additional adjustments in 37 
subsequent quarters. 38 
3. High -cost placements. A separate allocation must be determined for high -cost 39 
special education placements for children eligible under Part B, Section 619 in accordance 40 
with this subsection. 41 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 179 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
A. For high -cost, in-district placements, additional funds must be allocated for each 1 
student estimated to cost more than 2 times the statewide special education preschool 2 
per-pupil rate. The additional funds for each student must equal the amount by which 3 
that student's estimated costs exceed 2 times the statewide special education preschool 4 
per-pupil rate. 5 
B. For private school placements, additional funds must be allocated for each st udent 6 
estimated to cost 4 times the statewide special education preschool per-pupil rate. The 7 
additional funds for each student must equal the amount by which that student's 8 
estimated costs exceed 4 times the statewide special education preschool per-pupil rate. 9 
C. For public school, out-of-district placements, additional funds must be allocated for 10 
each student estimated to cost 3 times the statewide special education preschool per -11 
pupil rate. The additional funds for each student must equal the amount by which that 12 
student's estimated costs exceed 3 times the statewide special education preschool per-13 
pupil rate. 14 
D. For public regional special education program placements, additional funds must be 15 
allocated for each student estimated to cost 2 times the sta tewide special education 16 
preschool per-pupil rate. The additional funds for each student must equal the amount 17 
by which that student's estimated costs exceed 2 times the statewide special education 18 
preschool per-pupil rate. 19

Services System shall assist in maintaining education programming at special purpose 8 
private preschools by providing intermediate payments for specially designed instruction 9 
provided by each special purpose private preschool at a rate of $125 per day, per child 10 
receiving medically necessary therapeutic services through t he MaineCare program for 11 
scheduled school days in accordance with a child's individualized education program.  The 12 
Department of Education and the Child Development Services System shall make the 13 
payments for specially designed instruction provided by special purpose private preschools 14 
from July 1, 2024 to June 30, 2025. 15

Sec. DD-2.  5 MRSA c. 310-B is enacted to read: 10 
CHAPTER 310-B 11 
MAINE OFFICE OF COMMUNITY AFFAIRS 12 
§3201.  Definitions 13 
As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise indicates, the following terms 14 
have the following meanings.  15 
1.  Director.   "Director" means the Director of the Maine Office of Community Affairs 16 
appointed pursuant to section 3203. 17 
2.  Office.    "Office" means the Maine Office of Community Affairs established by 18 
section 3202. 19 
§3202.  Office established; purpose 20 
The Maine Office of Community Affairs is established as an agency in the  executive 21 
branch to foster communications and partnerships between the State and communities in 22 
this State. The office shall engage with municipalities, tribal governments and regional 23 
councils to provide coordinated and efficient planning, technical assi stance and financial 24 
support to better plan for challenges, pursue solutions and create stronger, more resilient 25 
communities. 26 
The office is established to partner with communities in this State and regional councils 27 
by: 28 
1. Assistance  and funding. Providing technical assistance and funding related to 29 
planning to municipalities, tribal governments and regional councils that supports a 30 
sustainable future for the State's people, communities, natural resources, physical 31 
infrastructure, industries, businesses and institutions; and 32 
2. Coordination and communication. Facilitating general coordination and 33 
communication between municipalities, tribal governments, regional councils and State 34 
Government. 35 
§3203.  Director 36 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 184 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
The Director of the Maine Office of Community Affairs is appointed by the Governor 1 
and serves at the pleasure of the Governor.  The director must have demonstrated 2 
experience and leadership in municipal or regional government and must bring expertise 3 
in planning, technical assistance and grant programs for communities. 4 
§3204.  Powers and duties 5 
The director shall exercise the powers of the office and is responsible for the execution 6 
of the duties of the office. 7 
1.  Duties of director.  The director shall: 8 
A.  Appoint and remove office staff and prescribe staff duties as necessary to 9 
implement the duties of the office, including: 10 
(1)  Hiring professional staff that have education, tr aining and experience in the 11 
fields of planning and development, local and regional government, climate 12 
science and resilience, housing, building codes and general policy making; and 13 
(2)  Employing additional staff as necessary to support the work of the office; 14 
B.  Supervise and administer the affairs of the office and advise the Governor and other 15 
officials of State Government on matters of communication and partnerships between 16 
the State, municipalities, tribal governments and regional councils in this State; 17 
C.  At the request of the Governor, act for the State in the initiation of or participation 18 
in any multigovernmental agency program related to the purposes of the office; 19 
D.  At the request of the Governor, prepare and submit a budget for the office; and 20 
E. At the request of the Governor, report on the activities of the office and, after 21 
consultation with and approval by the Governor, submit recommendations for 22 
legislative action as are determined necessary to further the purposes of this chapter. 23 
2.  Duties of office.  Under the supervision of the director, the office shall: 24 
A.  Provide technical assistance and resources to municipalities, tribal governments 25 
and regional councils on issues related to planning, climate resilience and development; 26 
B.  Collect and collate data and statistics relating to the issues described in paragraph 27 
A and provide them to municipalities, tribal governments and regional councils; 28 
C.  Assist municipalities, tribal governments and regional councils, as well as the State, 29 
in applying for, using and leveraging federal funding resources on issues of importance 30 
to communities and the State; 31 
D.  Make grants from money appropriated to the office by the Legislature and any 32 
funds received by the office for the purposes of the office, including federal funding or 33 
private funds; solicit applications for grants; and make grant awards to eligible 34 
communities and to service provider organizations as determined by the office, 35 
including establishing eligibility requirements and other crit eria to consider in 36 
awarding grants; 37 
E. Administer contracts with regional councils and regional planning and development 38 
districts to pr ovide technical assistance and resources to municipalities and tribal 39 
governments on issues related to planning, climate resilience and development, 40 
including but not limited to land use planning, planning for housing and other 41 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 185 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
residential development, climate resilience planning and related infrastructure 42 
planning, building codes and other forms of local development assistance to support 43 
state, regional and local goals; and44 
F. Consult with and provide ongoing coordination with state agencies on programs and 4 
issues related to planning technical assistance and funding to communities in this State, 5 
including but not limited to the Department of Transportation; Department of 6 
Environmental Protection; Department of Marine Resources; Department of  Inland 7 
Fisheries and Wildlife; Department of Agriculture, Conservation and Forestry; 8 
Department of Economic and Community Development; Department of Health and 9 
Human Services; Department of Defense, Veterans and Emergency Management, 10 
Maine Emergency Manag ement Agency; Department of Public Safety; Maine State 11 
Housing Authority; Governor's Energy Office; Efficiency Maine Trust; the Maine 12 
Historic Preservation Commission; and the Maine Redevelopment Land Bank 13 
Authority. 14 
§3205.  Acceptance and administration of funds 15 
The office may accept, administer and expend funds, including but not limited to funds 16 
from the Federal Government or from private sources, for purposes consistent with this 17 
chapter.  The director shall provide a report of the amount of any outside funding received 18 
from private sources and its designated purpose to the Governor and the joint standing 19 
committee of the Legislature having jurisdiction over municipal matters on an annual basis. 20 
§3206.  Contracts; agreements 21 
The office may employ expert and professional consultants, contract for services as the 22 
director determines necessary within the limits of the funds provided and consistent with 23 
the powers and duties of the office and enter into agreements with the Federal Government 24 
and other agencies and organizations that promote the objectives of this chapter. 25

Sec. FF-1.  5 MRSA §3110 is enacted to read: 39 
§3110.  Office of New Americans 40 
1. Establishment; purpose; administration.   The Office of New Americans is 41 
established within the Office of Policy Innovation and the Future for the purpose of 42 
improving the economic and civic integration of immigrants into the State's workforce and 43 
1 
2 
3 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 186 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
communities to strengthen the economy over the long term. The Office of Policy 44 
Innovation and the Future shall administer the Office of New Americans.45 
2. Director; duties. The director of the Office of New Americans shall fulfill the duties 3 
and activities listed in this section: 4 
A. Hiring professional personnel competent by education, training and experience to 5 
carry out the work of the Office of New Americans; 6 
B. Supervising and administering the affairs of the Office of New Americans; 7 
C. Determining the necessary budget for the Office of New Americans; and 8 
D. Reporting on the activities of the Office of New Americans. 9 
3. Duties of the Office of New Americans.   Under the supervision of the director of 10 
the Office of Policy Innovation and the Future and the director of the Office of New 11 
Americans, and with guidance from the Office of New Americans Advisory Council 12 
established in section 3111, the Office of New Americans shall identify and address needs, 13 
barriers and opportunities in order to support the long-term economic and civic integration 14 
of immigrants in the State by: 15 
A. Collecting and analyzing relevant data; 16 
B. Coordinating with all relevant local, state and federal government agencies; 17 
C. Serving as the State's primary liaison with all relevant external stakeholders; and 18 
D. Undertaking and promoting activities that improve the econ omic and civic 19 
integration of immigrants into the State's workforce and communities. 20 
4. Activities.  The Office of New Americans shall undertake and promote activities 21 
that improve the economic and civic integration of immigrants into the State's workforce 22 
and communities. Activities may include, but are not limited to: 23 
A. Strengthening workforce opport unities by providing guidance and promoting 24 
improved pathways for professional accreditation and licensure, supporting enhanced 25 
career pathways and engaging with businesses to increase employment, retention and 26 
advancement of immigrant employees; 27 
B. Expanding, improving and increasing access to English language learning programs;  28 
C. Strengthening financial literacy programs, financial education and entrepreneurship 29 
supports to assist individuals, immigrant entrepreneurs and small business owners; 30 
D. Supporting the expansion of access to legal services and protections; 31 
E. Partnering with and supporting municipalities, school administrative units, 32 
educational institutions, community -based organizations and businesses providing 33 
assistance or opportunities to immigrants; 34 
F. Participating in the nationwide Office of New Americans State Network, or its 35 
successor network, to access information and best practices from other states; 36 
G. Collaborating with and providing guidance to agencies of State Government and the 37 
entity designated by the Federal Government to administer the State's refugee 38 
resettlement services in developing and executing policies that support the purpose of 39 
the Office of New Americans; 40

2

H. Coordinating with and advising federal agencies and the State's congressional 1

of New Americans; and 5 
J. Promoting greater understanding of the history of immigration in the State, the 6

Sec. FF-2.  5 MRSA §3111 is enacted to read: 17 
§3111.  Office of New Americans Advisory Council 18 
The Office of New Americans Advisory Council, as established in section 12004 -I, 19 
subsection 6 -K, is created as an advisory council to the Office of New Americans 20 
established in section 3110 on matters affecting the long -term economic and civic 21 
integration of immigrants in the State. 22 
1. Duties of advisory council.  The advisory council shall advise the Office of New 23 
Americans on matters affecting the long-term economic and civic integration of immigrants 24 
in the State. 25 
2. Membership. The advisory council consists of 24 members as follows: 26 
A. Two members of the Senate, appointed by the President of the Senate, including a 27 
member fr om each of the 2 parties holding the largest number of seats in the 28 
Legislature; 29 
B. Two members of the House of Representatives, appointed by the Speaker of the 30 
House, including a member from each of the 2 parties holding the largest number of 31 
seats in the Legislature; 32 
C. Three members appointed by the President of the Senate representing the following: 33 
(1) A school administrative unit; 34 
(2) An adult education program; and 35 
(3)  A small business; 36 
D.  Three members appointed by the Speaker of the House representing the following: 37 
(1)  An organization providing refugee resettlement services; 38 
(2)  A provider of legal assistance to immigrants; and 39 
(3)  A municipality;  40 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 188 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
E. At least 10 members who are immigrants, 8 appointed by the Governor, one 1 
appointed by the President of the Senate and one appointed by the Speaker of the 2 
House; and 3 
F.  Four members appointed by the Governor representing the following: 4 
(1)  A large business; 5 
(2) A business or organization with demonstrated expertise in housing assistance 6 
or housing production; 7 
(3)  An organization with demonstrated expertise in workforce development; and  8 
(4) An employer with demonstrated experience providing immigrant 9 
apprenticeship opportunities, support and training programs. 10 
In making appointments of members to the advisory council, the appointing authorities 11 
shall make a good faith effort to ensure that the members of the advisory coun cil reflect 12 
geographic, gender, ethnic and racial diversity. 13 
3. Terms of office; removal.   Legislative members of the advisory council serve a 14 
term not to exceed their term in office, except that a legislative member may be appointed 15 
for successive terms.  Nonlegislative members serve 3-year terms and may be reappointed. 16 
A vacancy for an unexpired term must be filled in accordance with subsection 2. A member 17 
may serve until a replacement is appointed. The Governor may terminate the membership 18 
of any appointee for good cause. The reason for the termination must be communicated in 19 
writing to a member whose membership is terminated. The membership of any member 20 
must be terminated if the member is absent from 3 consecutive meetings without 21 
communicating good cause to a chair of the advisory council. 22 
4. Cochairs.   The Governor shall appoint 2 cochairs from among the members 23 
appointed and serving pursuant to subsection 2. 24 
5. Meetings; staffing.  The advisory council shall meet at the discretion of the cochairs. 25 
Meetings may be cancelled or postponed at the discretion of the cochairs. All meetings of 26 
the advisory council are public proceedings within the meaning of Title 1, chapter 13, 27 
subchapter 1. The Office of New Americans shall provide staffing services as necessary to 28 
the advisory council. 29 
6.  Compensation; expenses.   Members of the advisory council not otherwise 30 
compensated by their employer or the entity they represent for their time serving on the 31 
council may be compensated for their time and reimbursed for e xpenses, to the extent 32 
resources are available. The Office of New Americans shall determine the amount and 33 
manner of compensation and reimbursement for expenses. 34

§1812-I.  State approval for critical access hospitals; annual report required 19 
For purposes of this section, "critical access hospital" has the same meaning as in 20 
section 7932, subsection 10. 21 
1.  Application for conversion to critical access hospital.  In addition to the criteria 22 
provided in section 7932, subsection 10, in order to qualify as a critical access hospital, an 23 
applicant seeking approval for conversion to a critical access hospital must provide to the 24 
department a plan for review that includes the following: 25 
A.  A copy of the applicant's most recent community health needs assessment; 26 
B.  An estimate of the financial impact of converting to a critical access hospital; and 27 
C.  A utilization plan that includes the amount of total anticipated revenues that will be 28 
used and how they will be used to address the community health needs identified in the 29 
applicant's most recent assessment submitted pursuant to p aragraph A that are not 30 
currently being met. 31 
2.  Annual report by approved critical access hospitals.  A critical access hospital 32 
approved under this section shall provide an annual report to the department for a period 33 
of 5 years demonstrating its use of revenues to support the health care needs of the 34 
community. 35

Sec. MM-1.  22 MRSA §1730 is enacted to read: 29 
§1730.  Upper payment limits for aggregate MaineCare payments to hospitals 30 
1. Definitions. As used in this section, the following terms have the following 31 
meanings. 32 
A.  "Group of hospitals" means a group of hospitals in which each hospital meets the 33 
requirements for the same category of facility as described in 42 Code of Federal 34 
Regulations, Section 447.272 or 447.321. 35

PART ZZ 19 
Sec. ZZ-1.  26 MRSA §632-A is enacted to read: 20 
§632-A.  Fund for recovered wages 21 
1. Fund established.  The Wage Recovery Fund is esta blished as a nonlapsing fund 22 
within the bureau.  The purpose of the fund is to facilitate payments related to unpaid 23 
wages, unpaid health benefits, liquidated damages or interest owed to employees or former 24 
employees of an employer when the Department of L abor receives payments from an 25 
employer in accordance with a settlement agreement or a judgment on behalf of affected 26 
employees or former employees. 27 
2. Administration. The fund is administered by the director. Payment of unpaid wages, 28 
unpaid health benefits, liquidated damages or interest to affected individuals may be made 29 
only to the extent that the Department of Labor receives payment from the employer in 30 
accordance with a settlement agreement or a judgment.  The department is not liable for 31 
payments to affected individuals if the department does not receive the funds from the 32 
employer. 33 
3. Education.  As part of its settlement agreements, the Department of Labor may 34 
include a provision for payment of funds toward education and public messaging regarding 35 
the State's labor laws. Funds deposited in the Wage Recovery Fund that are not required 36 
for the payment of unpaid wages, unpaid health benefits, liquidated damages or interest 37 
may also be used for such education and public messaging. 38 
4. Fund balances.  Amounts in the Wage Recovery Fund do not lapse and must be 39 
carried forward to be used for the same purposes. Interest earned on the balance in the fund 40 
must be credited to the Wage Recovery Fund. 41

PART KKK 33 
Sec. KKK-1.  34-B MRSA §3613 is enacted to read: 34 
§3613.  Crisis receiving centers 35 
1.  Definition.  As used in this section, unless the context otherwise indicates, "crisis 36 
receiving center" means a center that provides immediate and short-term walk-in access to 37 
an array of both clinical and nonclinical mental health and substance use disorder crisis 38 
stabilization services to all individuals seeking care regardless of acuity or insurance 39 
coverage and within bounds of licensing. 40 
2.  Authority. The department shall develop a plan for a network of community-based 41 
crisis receiving centers across the State to su pport both clinical and nonclinical mental 42 
health and substance use disorder crisis stabilization services. The department shall also 43 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 201 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
coordinate meetings, technical assistance and training and provide other assistance to help 44 
create, maintain and, as necessary, expand the network.45 
3.  Guidelines.  The department shall: 3 
A. Consult with law enforcement agencies, municipalities, public health experts, 4 
behavioral health care providers, other states and others as appropriate; 5 
B. Assess geographical locations for maximization of community impact; 6 
C. Provide technical assistance to persons and entities across the State and providers 7 
interested in joining the network; 8 
D. Coordinate regular meetings with crisis receiving centers and provide technical 9 
assistance to crisis receiving centers; and 10 
E. Engage in continual process improvement and planning updates. 11

Sec. PPP -6. Recruitment and retention adjustment task force.   The 6 
Department of Administrative and Financial Services, Bureau of Human Resources shall 7 
convene a task force mediated by a neutral 3rd party to review and make recommendations 8 
regarding the criteria required under the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 5, section 7065, 9 
subsection 2-D for a recruitment and retention adjustment to be authorized. The task force 10 
must consist of one member from each of the 8 bargaining units of the executive branch, 11 
appointed by each unit's respective bargaining agent, and up to 8 additional members, 12 
appointed by the Governor. The task force must be cochaired by one member representing 13 
the State and one bargaining unit representative.  The cochairs must be selected by the 14 
membership of the task force. A state employee appointed to serve on the task force may 15 
participate in the work of the task force during the employee's r egular working hours 16 
without loss of pay or benefits.  By November 30, 2024, the task force shall complete the 17 
review and submit recommendations to the Department of Administrative and Financial 18 
Services, including draft legislation necessary to implement any proposed changes to the 19 
criteria for a recruitment and retention adjustment that are supported by a majority of the 20 
task force membership, and the department shall submit that proposed legislation to the 21 
First Regular Session of the 132nd Legislature. The task force shall meet once per month 22 
or as necessary to complete its work. 23

PART YYY 3 
Sec. YYY-1.  38 MRSA §480-KK is enacted to read: 4 
§480-KK.  Coastal Sand Dune Restoration and Protection Fund 5 
1.  Fund established; purposes and administration.   The Coastal Sand Dune 6 
Restoration and Protection Fund, referred to in this section as "the fund," is established as 7 
a nonlapsing fund within the department from which the department may pay up to 50% of 8 
the eligible costs incurred in a project to restore, protect, conserve, nourish or revegetate a 9 
coastal sand dune system, except that eligible costs for projects relating to coastal sand 10 
dune systems and addressing technical assistance and public education may be paid up to 11 
100%.  The department may prioritize funding of projects that use nature -based or 12 
ecologically enhanced techniques for restoring, protecting, conserving, nourishing or 13 
revegetating a coastal sand dune system.  Any balance remaining in the fund must continue 14 
without lapse from year to year and remain available only for the purposes for which the 15 
fund is established. 16 
2.  Prohibited expenditures.  The department may not use money in the fund to fund 17 
projects in a coastal sand dune system where public access is not provided to the beach or 18 
waterfront area adjacent to the coastal sand dune system. 19 
3.  Staffing support.  The department may use money in the fund for staffing to support 20 
administration and implementation of activities authorized under this section. 21 
4.  Public education program.  The department may use money in the fund to develop 22 
a coordinated public education program related to coastal sand dune systems.   23 
5.  Funding sources.  The fund may receive money from any source, public or private. 24 
Sec. YYY -2.  Permitting of offshore wind terminal on Sears Island.   25 
Notwithstanding any provision of law or Department of Environmental Protection rule 26 
prohibiting the construction of new structures in a coastal  sand dune system, the 27 
Department of Environmental Protection is authorized to grant a permit under the Maine 28 
Revised Statutes, Title 38, section 480-D for construction of an offshore wind terminal on 29 
Sears Island in the Town of Searsport to be located on or that will otherwise impact the 30 
Sears Island jetty dune, as long as the project satisfies all other applicable permitting and 31 
licensing criteria under Title 35-A, chapter 34 and Title 38, chapter 3.  The department is 32 
not authorized to grant more than one permit under Title 38, section 480-D for construction 33 
of an offshore wind terminal on Sears Island in accordance with this section. 34 
For the purposes of this section, the following terms have the following meanings. 35 
1.  "Coastal sand dune system" has the same meaning as in Title 38, section 480 -B, 36 
subsection 1. 37 
2. "Offshore wind terminal" has the same meaning as in Title 35 -A, section 3410, 38 
subsection 1, paragraph D. 39 
3.  "Sears Island jetty dune" means a coastal sand dune system on Sears Island in the 40 
Town of Searsport that is approximately 4/10 of an acre in size and located south of and 41 
abutting the jetty on the western side of the isla nd on the parcel of land reserved for port 42

PART DDDD 10 
Sec. DDDD -1. Strengthen and expand mental health crisis intervention 11 
mobile response services.   The Department of Health and Human Services shall 12 
strengthen and expand mental health crisis intervention mobile response services in order 13 
to provide services 24 hours a day, 7 days a week.  The department shall provide for the 14 
incorporation of mobile outreach peer support specialists, certified intentional peer support 15 
specialists and reco very coaches, mental health law enforcement liaisons through 16 
behavioral health agencies and community debriefing and critical incident response 17 
services into the existing crisis services response system.  The department shall also provide 18 
for ancillary ser vices that are required components of mental health crisis intervention 19 
mobile response services.  The funding for these ancillary services must include travel costs 20 
to and from mobile face -to-face assessments not to exceed the federal per mile rate, 21 
reimbursement for travel time to and from mobile face -to-face assessments and 22 
reimbursement for time spent on telephone conferences with clients.  The department shall 23 
provide reimbursement for peer support services provided as mental health crisis 24 
intervention mobile response services under the MaineCare program. 25

PART EEEE 9 
Sec. EEEE-1.  34-B MRSA §3613 is enacted to read: 10 
§3613.  Crisis receiving centers 11 
1. Definitions.  As used in this section, unless the context otherwise indicates, the 12 
following terms have the following meanings. 13 
A.  "Crisis receiving center" means a center providing walk-in access to crisis services 14 
to individuals experiencing behavioral health, ment al health and substance use 15 
challenges. 16 
B.  "Culturally sensitive trauma -informed care" means care that acknowledges, 17 
respects and integrates the cultural values, beliefs and practices of individuals and 18 
families. 19 
2.  Crisis receiving centers.  The department shall establish 2 crisis receiving centers 20 
to support individuals dealing with behavioral health, mental health or substance use issues.  21 
The receiving centers must be established in Aroostook County and Penobscot County.  22 
The department shall ensure t hat the crisis receiving centers provide culturally sensitive 23 
trauma-informed care.  The department shall develop a plan to expand crisis receiving 24 
centers statewide, with at least one crisis receiving center located in each county of the 25 
State. 26 
3.  Rules.  The department may adopt rules to implement this section.  Rules adopted 27 
pursuant to this subsection are routine technical rules as defined in Title 5, chapter 375, 28 
subchapter 2-A. 29

PART FFFF 26 
Sec. FFFF-1.  22 MRSA c. 256-B is enacted to read: 27 
CHAPTER 256-B 28 
OFFICE OF VIOLENCE PREVENTION 29 
§1427.  Office of Violence Prevention 30 
1.  Office established.  The Office of Violence Prevention, referred to in this section 31 
as "the office," is established within the Maine Center for Disease Control and Prevention 32 
to coordinate and promote effective efforts to reduce violence in the State, including, but 33 
not limited to, gun violence, and related trauma and promote research regarding causes of 34 
and evidence-based responses to violence, including gun violence. 35 
2.  Director.  The commissioner shall appoint the director of the office. 36 
3.  Collaboration.  To carry out its duties, the office may collaborate with other state 37 
agencies and programs, including, but not limited to, the Address Confidentiality Program 38 
established under Title 5, section 90-B; the Victims' Compensation Board established under 39 
3 
4 
5 
6 
7 
10 
11 
12 
13 
14 
15

COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 216 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
Title 5, section 3360 -A; the Department of Education; the Office of Behavioral Health 40 
established under Title 5, section 20011; the Office of the Attorney General; the 41 
Department of Public Safety; the Maine Bureau of Veterans' Services established under 42 
Title 37-B, section 501; and the violence prevention program within the department.43 
4.  Awareness and education.  The office shall increase the awareness of and educate 5 
the general public about laws and resources relating to violence prev ention and conduct 6 
awareness and education campaigns in accordance with this subsection. 7 
A.  The office shall increase the awareness of and educate the general public about state 8 
and federal laws and existing resources relating to violence prevention, including: 9 
(1)  The availability of and the process for requesting protection orders, including, 10 
but not limited to, protection from abuse orders under Title 19-A, chapter 103 and 11 
protection from harassment orders under Title 5, chapter 337-A; 12 
(2)  The process for accessing available mental health and substance use disorder 13 
resources and how to refer individuals to needed mental health and substance use 14 
disorder treatment services, including suicide prevention services; 15 
(3)  The process for accessing available resources and services for domestic 16 
violence prevention; 17 
(4)  The process for reporting a lost or stolen firearm, including reporting 18 
requirements in state law; 19 
(5)  The best practices for safe storage of firearms; and 20 
(6)  Safe and responsible gun ownership, including increased awareness of the law 21 
and methods of compliance with state and federal law. 22 
B.  The office shall conduct awareness and education campaigns and develop and 23 
provide educational materials and training resources, including: 24 
(1)  Developing and providing educational materials and training resources to local 25 
law enforcement agencies, health care providers and educators to assist those 26 
agencies, providers and educators with educating the public about the laws, 27 
available resources and effective violence prevention strategies; 28 
(2)  Conducting awareness and education campaigns in a culturally competent way, 29 
including by providing materials and resources in multiple languages;   30 
(3)  Conducting awareness and education campaigns directed toward gun owners, 31 
parents and legal guardians of children and organizations that provide services to 32 
individuals and communities disproportionately affected by gun violence; and 33 
(4)  At the request of the Director of the Maine Center for Disease Control and 34 
Prevention, supporting and providing assistance for education campaigns and 35 
programs conducted by the department that are related to gun violence, including 36 
education campaigns and programs relating to the safe storage of firearms and 37 
suicide prevention. 38 
The office may focus the awareness and education campaigns required under this 39 
paragraph in communities identified by the office as disproportionately affected by gun 40 
violence and use television messaging, radio broadcasts, print media, digital strategies 41 
1 
2 
3 
4 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 217 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
or any other form of messaging considered effective and appropriate by the office to 42 
achieve the goals of this section.43 
5.  Grant program.  Subject to available funding, the office may establish and 3 
administer a grant program to award grants to organizations to conduct community -based 4 
violence intervention initiatives that are primarily focused on interrupting cycles of 5 
violence, including gun violence, trauma and retaliation by providing culturally competent 6 
intervention services. 7 
A.  To be eligible for a grant award, an organization must demonstrate the ability to 8 
conduct effective community -based violence intervention initiatives t hat meet the 9 
criteria described in this subsection and in rules adopted by the Maine Center for 10 
Disease Control and Prevention. The office shall prioritize awarding grants to 11 
organizations that conduct violence intervention initiatives with individuals and  in 12 
communities identified as having the highest imminent risk of perpetrating or being 13 
victimized by violence. 14 
B.  An initiative conducted with a grant award must use strategies that are evidence -15 
informed and have demonstrated potential for reducing viole nce without contributing 16 
to mass incarceration, such as group violence interventions, evidence-based street and 17 
community outreach programs, violence interruption and crisis management programs 18 
and individualized wraparound services. To improve the effecti veness of a violence 19 
intervention initiative, a grant recipient shall conduct regular evaluations of the 20 
initiative, including community input and engagement. 21 
C.  The Maine Center for Disease Control and Prevention shall adopt rules necessary 22 
for the admin istration of the grant program, including grant application procedures, 23 
criteria for determining the amount and duration of the grants and reporting 24 
requirements for organizations that receive grants. 25 
D.  In administering the grant program, the office shal l collaborate with stakeholders 26 
as needed to ensure equity in the distribution of grants.  The office shall consult with 27 
stakeholders to develop grant priorities. Stakeholders must include individuals and 28 
families affected by violence, organizations with expertise in violence prevention and 29 
gun safety and representatives of communities of color. 30 
E.  By February 1, 2027, the department shall submit to the joint standing committee 31 
of the Legislature having jurisdiction over health and human services matters a report 32 
that includes the following: 33 
(1)  Information regarding the number of grants awarded and the amount of funding 34 
provided to each grant recipient; 35 
(2)  A description of violence intervention initiatives funded, including the number 36 
of individuals served and the communities served by each funded initiative; and 37 
(3)  Recommendations regarding the continuation of the grant program and 38 
recommendations for any changes to the program. 39 
F.  This subsection is repealed June 30, 2027. 40 
6.  Data hub.  The office shall create and maintain a data hub of regularly updated and 41 
accurate materials and resources as a repository for data, research an d statistical 42 
1 
2 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214

COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
information regarding violence in the State, including gun violence. As part of maintaining 43 
the data hub, the office shall:44 
A.  Assist researchers who are seeking information regarding violence in the State; 3 
B.  Collaborate with resear chers, including organizations that conduct gun violence 4 
research, to: 5 
(1)  Identify gaps in available data needed to conduct violence prevention research 6 
and develop strategies to improve relevant data collection in the State; 7 
(2)  Use existing available research to enhance evidence-based violence prevention 8 
tools and resources available to communities in the State; and 9 
(3)  Improve the understanding of the disproportionate barriers to safety from 10 
violence by encouraging disaggregation of data by race and ethnicity when 11 
research is conducted; and 12 
C.  Promote new and relevant research regarding violence prevention and, if possible, 13 
make the research accessible to researchers and the public. 14 
7.  Reporting requirements.   The office and the department shall pro vide the 15 
following reports relating to the office's work. 16 
A.  Annually, by November 30th, the office shall report to the department on the 17 
activities it has conducted in the preceding 12 months. The report must include: 18 
(1)  Information regarding awareness  and education campaigns conducted by the 19 
office; 20 
(2)  Effective violence intervention programs identified by the office; 21 
(3)  Any federal grants or other funding the office applied for and whether the 22 
office received those grants or other funds; 23 
(4)  A general summary of new and relevant research included in the office's data 24 
hub under subsection 6 and the nature of research assistance provided by the office; 25 
and 26 
(5)  Recommendations to enhance the administration and operation of the office 27 
and improve the availability of services to reduce violence in the State. 28 
The office shall make the report available on its publicly accessible website or on the 29 
Maine Center for Disease Control and Prevention's publicly accessible website.   30 
B.  In its annual report to the joint standing committee of the Legislature having 31 
jurisdiction over health and human services matters pursuant to section 1425, the 32 
Maine Center for Disease Control and Prevention shall include a summary of the 33 
office's annual report submitted under paragraph A, including recommendations under 34 
paragraph A, subparagraph (5) and instructions for accessing any new and relevant 35 
violence prevention research identified by the office in paragraph A, subparagraph (4). 36 
The Maine Center for Disease Control and P revention shall make the summary 37 
available on its publicly accessible website. 38 
8.  Rules.  The Maine Center for Disease Control and Pre vention shall adopt rules to 39 
implement this chapter.  Rules adopted pursuant to this subsection are major substantive 40 
rules as defined in Title 5, chapter 375, subchapter 2-A. 41

§2015.  Gun shop project 33 
1.  Definitions.   As used in this section, unless the context otherwise indicates, the 34 
following terms have the following meanings. 35 
A.  "Dangerous or deadly weapon" has the same meaning as "dangerous weapon" in 36 
Title 17-A, section 2, subsection 9, paragraph C. 37 
B.  "Department" means the Department of Public Safety. 38 
C.  "Firearm" has the same meaning as in Title 17-A, section 2, subsection 12-A. 39

D.  "Gun shop" means a business located in the State that sells firearms, dangerous or 1 
deadly weapons or related components such as ammunition. 2 
E.  "Gun shop project" means a project to develop, create and distribute suicide 3 
prevention educational materials. 4 
2.  Administration of gun shop project.  The department shall administer a gun shop 5 
project. 6 
3.  Development and creation of educational materials ; online training .  In 7 
administering a gun shop project under this section, t he department shall contract with a 8 
statewide organization with expertise in mental health for the development and creation of 9 
suicide prevention educational materials, including an online training course. 10 
A.  Educational materials under this subsection mu st include but are not limited to 11 
information on: 12 
(1)  Understanding and recognizing the various clinical signs, symptoms and 13 
indicators of suicide risk; and 14 
(2)  Available suicide prevention resources. 15 
B.  In developing and creating educational materials under this subsection, the 16 
contracted statewide organization must refer to the following: 17 
(1)  Gun shop projects in other states; 18 
(2)  Programs created or offered by organizations in the dangerous or deadly 19 
weapon industry; and 20 
(3)  Other projects or organizations that the department determines appropriate. 21 
C.  Educational materials under this subsection must be created as written materials, 22 
such as pamphlets, signs, posters, tip sheets or other media, and as an online training 23 
course for firearm dealers li censed as dealers under 18 United States Code, Section 24 
923(a)(3) and gun shop customers. 25 
4.  Distribution of gun shop project educational materials.   The department shall 26 
ensure that the written educational materials and online training course created unde r 27 
subsection 3 are available on the department's publicly accessible website. 28 
Sec. HHHH-2. Reporting requirement. By December 1, 2026, the Department 29 
of Public Safety shall submit a written report regarding the activities during the prior 30 
calendar year related to the development and administration of the gun shop project under 31 
the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 25, section 2015, including, but not limited to, the 32 
categories of educational materials developed, the different types of written educational 33 
materials created and the number of participants in the online training course, to the joint 34 
standing committee of the Legislature having jurisdiction over public safety matters. 35

PART KKKK 29 
Sec. KKKK-1.  30-A MRSA c. 201, sub-c. 14 is enacted to read: 30 
SUBCHAPTER 14 31 
SUBSIDY PROGRAM FOR HOMELESS STUDENTS 32 
§4994-A. Subsidy program for homeless students 33 
1. Definitions.  As used in this section, unless the context otherwise indicates, the 34 
following terms have the following meanings. 35 
A. "Elementary school" has the same meaning as in Title 20 -A, section 1, subsection 36 
10. 37 
4 
5 
6 
7 
8 
19 
20 
21 
22 
23 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 223 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
B. "Homeless student" has the same meaning as in Title 20 -A, section 1, subsection 1 
13-A. 2 
C. "Secondary school" has the same meaning as in Title 20 -A, section 1, subsection 3 
32. 4 
2. Program established.  The Maine State Housing Authority shall establish a housing 5 
subsidy program for homeless students in elementary school and seco ndary school.  The 6 
authority shall adopt rules to implement this program.  Rules adopted pursuant to this 7 
subsection are routine technical rules as defined in Title 5, chapter 375, subchapter 2-A. 8 
Sec. KKKK -2.  Subsidy program development.   The Maine State Housing 9 
Authority, referred to in this section as "the authority, " shall develop a rental subsidy 10 
program for homeless students in coordination with the Department of Education and the 11 
Department of Health and Human Services and other agenc ies or service providers as the 12 
authority determines appropriate.  The authority shall consider ways in which the services 13 
provided by school-based housing navigators established by the federal McKinney-Vento 14 
Homeless Assistance Act could benefit the administration of a rental subsidy program.  The 15 
program must provide housing subsidies directly to homeless students or to an adult family 16 
member or guardian of the homeless student.  In developing the program, the authority 17 
shall incorporate elements to provide housing subsidies to homeless students who have not 18 
attained 18 years of age who do not have adult family members or guardians to secure 19 
housing on their behalf.  The authority shall report to the joint standing or joint select 20 
committee of the Legislat ure having jurisdiction over housing matters on the progress of 21 
the program's development no later than January 15, 2025. 22 
Sec. KKKK-3.  Maine State Housing Authority to develop pilot program.   23 
The Maine State Housing Authority shall establish a pilot progr am designed to provide 24 
support for eviction prevention. The pilot program must be designed to provide eligible 25 
persons with up to $800 per month in rental assistance paid directly to the person's landlord 26 
for a period of up to 24 months.  Assistance receiv ed under this program is not income or 27 
an asset for the purposes of determining eligibility for or the benefit amount to be paid from 28 
any public assistance program administered by the State or by a municipality pursuant to 29 
the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 22, chapter 1161.  Persons eligible for rental assistance: 30 
1.  Must earn less than 60% of the median income for the area as defined by the United 31 
States Department of Housing and Urban Development under the United States Housing 32 
Act of 1937, Public Law 75-412, 50 Stat. 888, Section 8, as amended;  33 
2.  May not, at the time of application to the pilot program, be using a federal housing 34 
voucher to pay rent or live in a subsidized housing unit; 35 
3.  Must provide proof of a current landlord-tenant relationship such as a lease or other 36 
documentation sufficient to demonstrate a landlord-tenant relationship to the administrative 37 
entity of the pilot program; and 38 
4.  Must have a rental payment within 125% of the fair market rental payment amount 39 
of the housing authority of jurisdiction. 40 
The Maine State Housing Authority shall delegate administration of the pilot program 41

altered elevators and tramways are not subject to a $500 cap applied to other fees related 32

to change fees associated with elevator inspections to cover the costs of additional Elevator 37
