PART F 3 
This Part updates the definition of "biennial base year appropriation " for the laws 4 
governing the General Fund appropriation limitation and clarifies that when the Maine 5 
Budget Stabilization Fund is at its statutory limit funds transferred from the General Fund 6 
to the Irrevocable Trust Funds for Other Post -employment Benefits are for the trust fund 7 
established for the state employee retiree health plan. 8 
This Part also increases the biennial base year appropriation, for fiscal year 2024 -25 9 
only, to 99% of the baseline General Fund revenue. 10 
PART G 11 
This Part provides that, beginning in the school year starting after June 30, 2025, the 12 
minimum hourly wage for educational technicians is 125% of the state minimum hourly 13 
wage and the minimum hourly wage for other school support staff who are paid hourly is 14 
115% of the state minimum hourly wage. If the state minimum hourly wage is increased 15 
on January 1st of any year, the minimum hourly wage for educational technicians and other 16 
school support staff is increased beginning July 1st of the same year.   17 
This Part provides that, beginning in fiscal year 2025-26 and for each subsequent fiscal 18 
year, the Commissioner of Education is required to update the salary matrix to reflect any 19 
increase in the minimum hourly wage of educational technicians and other school support 20 
staff.  The Department of Education is directed to incorporate the minimum hourly wage 21 
into the essential programs and services funding model. 22 
This Part also provides that, for the 2025 -2026 school year only, the State must pay 23 
100% of the additional funding necessary to achieve the minimum hourly wage. 24 
PART H 25 
This Part changes the approach to the taxation of rental property from imposing sales 26 
and use tax on the lessor upfront on the purchase price of the rental property to instead 27 
imposing tax on l ease or rental payments going forward, also known as the lease stream.  28 
Under lease stream taxation, the lessor is required to collect and remit sales or use tax from 29 
the lessee on each rental payment.  This Part provides a limited time period in which a 30 
lessor who has paid sales or use tax on the purchase of rental property that is now subject 31 
to lease stream taxation may claim a refund. The changes apply to sales, leases and rentals 32 
on or after January 1, 2025.   This Part also provides an exemption from the sales and use 33 
tax to nonprofit organizations that are exempt from federal income taxation pursuant to 34 
Section 501(c)(3) of the United States Internal Revenue Code of 1986. 35 
PART I 36 
This Part requires the State Controller to carry forward up to $750,000 of unexpended 37 
balance in the Capital Expenditures line category in the Department of Agriculture, 38 
Conservation and Forestry, Bureau of Agriculture program, General Fund account the end 39 
of fiscal year 2023-24 to upgrade the Cony Road facility in Augusta. 40

PART N 25 
This Part creates the Maine Mass Violence Care Fund in the Department of the 26 
Attorney General to provide financial support to victims of mass violence crimes and their 27 
families and household members.  The financial support is f or out -of-pocket costs for 28 
physical and behavioral health care not otherwise paid for by insurance or some other 29 
source.  The Treasurer of State is directed to administer the fund in a manner consistent 30 
with investment standards established in the Maine Uniform Trust Code. 31 
When the underlying crime is a mass violence crime, payments may be made from the 32 
existing Victims' Compensation Fund but all payments in excess of the $15,000 limit on 33 
payments from the Victims' Compensation Fund must be made from the Ma ine Mass 34 
Violence Care Fund. 35 
The Maine Mass Violence Care Fund is funded by an initial transfer of $5,000,000 36 
from the General Fund unappropriated surplus.  Disbursements from the fund are made by 37 
the Victims' Compensation Board within the Department of the Attorney General but may 38 
only be from the earnings on the fund or from donations to the fund. 39 
This Part also creates a working group to  recommend changes to eligibility standards 40 
with regard to distributions from the fund as established by the Victims' Compensation 41 
Board. 42

PART W 1 
This Part reorganizes oversight and updates practices for serving infants, toddlers and 2 
children with disabilities from birth to 6 years of age. This Part: 3 
1.  Establishes the extended Part C option under the federal Individuals with 4 
Disabilities Education Act to continue individualized family service plans until the start of 5 
the school year when the child is 4 years of age if the family chooses; 6 
2. Provides that, beginning July 1, 2028, all school administrative units are responsible 7 
for child find activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education for children 8 
eligible under Part B, Section 619 of the federal Individu als with Disabilities Education 9 
Act; 10 
3. Provides that, until June 30, 2028, the Commissioner of Education is required to 11 
designate responsibility for child find activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public 12 
education for eligible children to the C hild Development Services System or to school 13 
administrative units in accordance with a transition schedule. During the transition, the 14 
commissioner may approve school administrative units to assume the responsibility for 15 
child find activities and for ensu ring a free, appropriate public education. The school 16 
administrative units must be provided professional learning and technical support and the 17 
department must assess and approve readiness plans. This Part adds to the duties of the 18 
director of early childh ood special education within the department to support the 19 
transition. The department is required to contract with a national expert to regularly monitor 20 
funding and programming, and report annually in March to the joint standing committee of 21 
the Legislature having jurisdiction over education matters. This Part also allows the Child 22 
Development Services System to appoint parental advisory committees at each of the 23 
regional support and service hubs. This Part also requires the Department of Education to 24 
designate an individual to coordinate the concurrent transition of responsibility for 25 
providing a free , appropriate public education to children eligible under the federal 26 
Individuals with Disabilities Education Act, Part B, Section 619 and for children 27 
participating in universal public-preschool in alignment  with the goals outlined in the 28 
Maine Revised Statutes, Title 20-A, section 4501; 29 
4. Establishes that school administrative units may provide services directly or may 30 
contract with public or private providers to provide services and that school administrative 31 
units may also access their Child Development Services System regional site or regional 32 
support and service hub to provide certain services. A memorandum of understanding must 33 
be developed between the s chool administrative unit and the Department of Education to 34 
determine the services to be provided by the regional support and service hub; 35 
5. Provides that, when school administrative units assume responsibility for child find 36 
activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education, the Child Development 37 
Services System will transition from a regional site to a regional support and service hub 38 
aligned with the 9 superintendent regions. This Part establishes the minimum requirements 39 
and guiding principles for the regional support and service hubs; 40 
6. Allows the Commissioner of Education to grant an additional year to school 41 
administrative units that require additional time and support to assume responsibility for 42 
child find activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education and provides that, 43 
if the commissioner determines that a school administrative unit is unable to assume 44

PART JJ 25 
This Part makes several changes to the laws governing the hospital tax. 26 
1.  It removes critical access hospitals from the definition of "hospital" beginning  27 
January 1, 2025. 28 
2.  It changes the tax imposed on hospitals from 2.23% to 3.25% beginning January 1, 29 
2025. 30 
3.  It specifies that the tax no longer applies to critical access hospitals beginning 31 
January 1, 2025. 32 
4.  Beginning January 1, 2025, it changes the taxable year for hospitals from 2020 to 33 
2022. 34 
5.  It clarifies that the changes beginning January 1, 2025 apply to the tax payment due 35 
on May 15, 2025. 36 
6.  It requires revenues received in each fiscal year from the hospital tax to be credited 37 
to the Medical Care - Payments to Providers Other Special Revenue Funds accou nt to be 38 
used for MaineCare hospital payments. 39 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “A” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 235 - 131LR3108(02) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
PART KK 1 
This Part requires an applicant seeking to convert a hospital into a critical access 2 
hospital to provide to the Department of Health and Human Services a copy of the 3 
applicant's most recent community health needs assessment, an estimate of the financial 4 
impact of converting to a critical access hospital and a utilization plan that includes the 5 
amount of total anticipated revenues that will be used and how they will be used to address 6 
the community health needs that are not being fully met at that time.  An approved critical 7 
access hospital must provide an annual report to the department for a period of 5 years 8 
demonstrating its use of revenues to support the health care needs of the community.   9 
Finally, this Part adds to the definition of "critical access hospital" a cross-reference to the 10 
new provisions of law enacted by this Part. 11 
PART LL 12 
This Part  amends the laws governing reimbursement to critical access hospitals as of 13 
January 1, 2025 by terminating the requirement that the Department of Health and Human 14 
Services allocate to critical access  hospitals for staff enhancement payments  at least 15 
$1,000,000 from hospital tax revenues collected under the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 16 
36, chapter 377 and $1,000,000 from hospital tax revenues collected under Title 36, chapter 17 
375. 18 
This Part also changes the reimbursement percentage to critical access hospitals from 19 
109% to 104.5% of MaineCare allowable costs beginning January 1, 2025. 20 
PART MM 21 
This Part requires the Department of Health and Human Services to ensure that 22 
aggregate MaineCare payments made  to a group of hospitals comply with the upper 23 
payment limit applicable to that group as required under federal regulations. Beginning 24 
July 1, 2024, if aggregate MaineCare payments to a group of hospitals exceed the 25 
applicable upper payment limit, the department shall limit payments to that group to ensure 26 
compliance. The department must share its calculations and data related to the upper 27 
payment limit with affected hospitals at least 60 days prior to taking any action. 28 
If the department limits payments to a group of hospitals and the Federal Government 29 
determines that the payments made to that group were below the upper payment limit 30 
applicable to that group, this Part also requires the department to increase payments to that 31 
group. 32 
PART NN 33 
This Part delays until July 1, 2024 the requirement that the Department of Health and 34 
Human Services establish income disregards for determining eligibility in the Medicare 35 
savings program. 36

Services, General Assistance - Reimbursement to Cities and Towns program, Other Special 40 
Revenue Funds account for funding general assistance payments to cities and towns. 41

PART QQQ 13 
This Part amends the provision of law that requires the Department of Health and 14 
Human Services to establish a substance use disorder treatment center in Kennebec County 15 
or Washington County. This Part specifies that the treatment center must be established in 16 
Kennebec County and that services offered by the center must be available to all individuals 17 
regardless of insurance. This Part also makes optional certain conditions that are required 18 
under the current law, including the condition that the treatment center have at least 10 beds 19 
and that the center offer medically managed withdrawal services. This Part also requires 20 
that the center offer services aligned with standards for crisis care developed by national 21 
mental health and substance use disorder organizations and the services offered by the crisis 22 
receiving center in Portland.  23 
Finally, this Part retroactively changes the date by which the department must award a 24 
contract for the development of the treatment center from the original deadline of 25 
December 1, 2023 to 90 days after the effective date of this Part. 26

PART ZZZ 28 
This Part amends the law governing paid family and medical leave.  This Part amends 29 
the defin ition of "base period" to reflect calendar quarters for which wage information 30 
would be available and amends the definition of "benefit year" to consider the date that 31 
leave begins in order to ensure parity between family and medical leave.  This Part repeals 32 
a provision of the paid family and medical leave benefit program that establishes criteria 33 
for evaluating bids to contract with a 3rd party for claims administration.  The procurement 34 
of a 3rd-party claims administrator is governed by the remaining relevant provisions of the 35 
paid family and medical leave benefits program and state procurement laws.  This Part 36 
amends intermittent leave requirements to reflect an individual's actual work day instead 37 
of a set 8 hours and clarifies that an employee and empl oyer may not agree to a reduced 38 
leave schedule that permits leave increments of less than one hour.  This Part increases the 39 
cap on the cost of administering the paid family and medical leave benefits program from 40 
5% to 10% of the amount deposited to the Paid Family and Medical Leave Insurance Fund 41 
for each fiscal year. 42

PART MMMM 5 
This Part requires the State Controller to transfer $23,535,428 from the unappropriated 6 
surplus of the General Fund to the MaineCare Stabilization Fund on or before June 30, 7 
2025.  This Part also requires the State Controller on or before June 30, 2025 to transfer 8 
from the available balance of the  unappropriated surplus of the General Fund up to 9 
$6,464,572 to the Department of Health and Human Services, MaineCare Stabilization 10 
Fund program, Other Special Revenue Funds account after other required transfers are 11 
made. 12 
PART NNNN 13 
This Part requires the Department of Health and Human Services to issue a request for 14 
proposals to develop one or more psychiatric residential treatment facilities in the State to 15 
meet the residential care needs of adolescents who have high levels of behav ioral health 16 
needs that cannot be met by existing behavioral health services in the State. 17 
PART OOOO 18 
This Part requires the State Controller to transfer $11,000,000 from the unallocated 19 
balance of the Highway Fund to the unappropriated surplus of the General Fund on or 20 
before June 30, 2025. 21 
PART PPPP 22 
This Part requires the transfer of $8,747,622 on or before June 30, 2025 from the 23 
unappropriated surplus of the General Fund to the Department of Health and Human 24 
Services, Office of Substance Abuse  and Mental Health Services program, Other Special 25 
Revenue Funds account for the purpose of providing emergency one-time assistance to St. 26 
Mary’s Regional Medical Center and for other emergency needs of the City of Lewiston  27 
associated with the mass casualty event on October 25, 2023. 28 
PART QQQQ 29 
This Part continues those limited -period positions that are proposed to continue in 30 
fiscal year 2024-25 but for which funding ends at the end of fiscal year 2023-24. 31 
PART RRRR 32 
This Part requires the Department of Heal th and Human Services to offer grants and 33 
incentives to providers to expand into rural areas to provide services to children and adults 34 
in families involved in the child welfare system. An appropriation of $500,000 in each year 35 
of the biennium is provided in Part A for this purpose. 36 
PART SSSS 37 
This Part requires the Department of Health and Human Services, Office of Behavioral 38 
Health to provide training to clinicians in the so -called assertive continuing care protocol 39 
to facilitate the delivery of the evidence-based practice for potential expansion of services 40 
for the acute mental health needs of adolescents with co-occurring disorders. 41
